         <a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">
          DST
         </a>
         )
        </span>
       </th>
       <td>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Daylight_Time" title="Pacific Daylight Time">
         Pacific Daylight Time
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%927" title="UTC−7">
         UTC−7
        </a>
        )
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr class="mergedtoprow">

        </a>

        </a>
        code
       </th>
       <td>
        06-029
       </td>
      </tr>

        </a>
        feature ID
       </th>
       <td>
        <a class="external text" href="http://geonames.usgs.gov/apex/f?p=gnispq:3:::NO::P3_FID:2054176" rel="nofollow">

        </a>
       </td>

      <tr class="mergedtoprow">
       <th scope="row">
        Website
       </th>
       <td>
        <span class="url">
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.co.kern.ca.us" rel="nofollow">
          www
          <wbr>
          </wbr>

          <wbr>

          <wbr>

          .us
         </a>
        </span>
       </td>

     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       Kern County
      </b>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">
       county
      </a>
      located in the
      <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
       U.S. state
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      . As of the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
       2010 census
      </a>
      , the population was 839,631.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-QF-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its
      <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">
       county seat
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_California" title="Bakersfield, California">
       Bakersfield
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GR6-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Kern County comprises the Bakersfield, CA
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
       Metropolitan Statistical Area
      </a>
      . The county spans the southern end of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Valley,_California" title="Central Valley, California">
       Central Valley
      </a>
      . Covering 8,161.42 square miles (21,138.0 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ), it ranges west to the southern slope of the
      <a href="/wiki/California_Coast_Ranges" title="California Coast Ranges">
       Coast Ranges
      </a>
      , and east beyond the southern slope of the eastern
      <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">
       Sierra Nevada
      </a>
      into the
      <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">
       Mojave Desert
      </a>
      , at the city of
      <a href="/wiki/Ridgecrest,_California" title="Ridgecrest, California">
       Ridgecrest
      </a>
      . Its northernmost city is
      <a href="/wiki/Delano,_California" title="Delano, California">
       Delano
      </a>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      and its southern reach expands just beyond
      <a href="/wiki/Lebec,_California" title="Lebec, California">
       Lebec
      </a>
      to the
      <a href="/wiki/Grapevine,_California" title="Grapevine, California">
       Grapevine
      </a>
      and the northern tip of the parallel
      <a href="/wiki/Antelope_Valley" title="Antelope Valley">
       Antelope Valley
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The county's economy is heavily linked to agriculture and to petroleum extraction. There is also a strong aviation, space, and military presence, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">
       Edwards Air Force Base
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Weapons_Station_China_Lake" title="Naval Air Weapons Station China Lake">
       China Lake Naval Air Weapons Station
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Air_and_Space_Port" title="Mojave Air and Space Port">
       Mojave Air and Space Port
      </a>
      . It is one of the fastest growing areas in the United States in terms of population growth, and suffers from significant water supply issues and poor air quality.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_era">
       Spanish era
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Spanish era">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The area was claimed by the Spanish in 1769, and in 1772 Commander
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Don_Pedro_Fages" title="Don Pedro Fages">
       Don Pedro Fages
      </a>
      became the first European to enter it, from the south by way of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grapevine_Canyon,_California" title="Grapevine Canyon, California">
       Grapevine Canyon
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Kern County was the site of the Battle of San Emigdio, in March 1824, between the
      <a href="/wiki/Chumash_people" title="Chumash people">
       Chumash
      </a>
      Indians of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_Mission" title="Santa Barbara Mission">
       Santa Barbara Mission
      </a>
      who rebelled against the Mexican government's taking over mission property and ejecting the natives. This battle with Mexican forces from
      <a href="/wiki/Monterey,_California" title="Monterey, California">
       Monterey
      </a>
      under the command of Carlos Carrillo took place at the canyon where San Emigdio Creek flows down
      <a href="/wiki/San_Emigdio_Mountains" title="San Emigdio Mountains">
       San Emigdio Mountain
      </a>
      and the Blue Ridge south of Bakersfield near today's Highway 166. It was a low-casualty encounter, with only four Indians killed, and no Mexicans; the surviving Indians were pacified and brought back to Santa Barbara in June 1824 after a pursuit and negotiation in which many were allowed to keep their arms for the return march over the mountains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="American_era">
       American era
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: American era">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1535" data-file-width="2309" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG/200px-Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG/300px-Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/34/Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG/400px-Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Havilah_CA_Courthouse_Museum.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Havilah Court building was restored in the 1970s and now serves as a museum. Photo circa 2007.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the beginning, the area that became Kern County was dominated by mining in the mountains and in the desert. In 1855 an attempt to form a county in the area was made when the California legislature took the southeastern territory of Tulare County on the west of the Sierra Nevada Mountains for
      <a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_County,_California" title="Buena Vista County, California">
       Buena Vista County
      </a>
      , but it was never officially organized prior to 1859, when the time of the enabling legislation ran out. The south of Tulare County was later organized as Kern County in 1866, with additions from Los Angeles and San Bernardino Counties. Its first county seat was in the mining town of
      <a href="/wiki/Havilah,_California" title="Havilah, California">
       Havilah
      </a>
      , in the mountains between Bakersfield and
      <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi,_California" title="Tehachapi, California">
       Tehachapi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The flatlands were considered inhospitable and impassable at the time due to swamps, lakes, tule reeds and diseases such as malaria. This changed when settlers started draining lands for farming and constructing canals, most dug by hand by hired Chinese laborers. Within 10 years the valley surpassed the mining areas as the economic center of the county, and the county seat was moved as a result from Havilah to Bakersfield in 1874.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The discovery well of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_River_Oil_Field" title="Kern River Oil Field">
       Kern River Oil Field
      </a>
      was dug by hand in 1899.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Soon the towns of
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_City,_California" title="Oil City, California">
       Oil City
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oil_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oil Center (page does not exist)">
       Oil Center
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oildale" title="Oildale">
       Oildale
      </a>
      came into existence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
       Etymology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Etymology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The county derives its name from the
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_River" title="Kern River">
       Kern River
      </a>
      , which was named for
      <a href="/wiki/Edward_Kern" title="Edward Kern">
       Edward Kern
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartographer" title="Cartographer">
       cartographer
      </a>
      for General
      <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frémont">
       John C. Frémont
      </a>
      's 1845 expedition, which crossed
      <a href="/wiki/Walker_Pass" title="Walker Pass">
       Walker Pass
      </a>
      . The Kern River was originally named Rio Bravo de San Felipe by Father Francisco Garces when he explored the area in 1776.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">
       Earthquakes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/1952_Kern_County_earthquake" title="1952 Kern County earthquake">
       1952 Kern County earthquake
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Severe earthquakes have struck Kern County within historical times, including the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Tejon_earthquake" title="Fort Tejon earthquake">
       Fort Tejon earthquake
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On
      <a href="/wiki/1952_Kern_County_earthquake" title="1952 Kern County earthquake">
       July 21, 1952, an earthquake
      </a>
      with the
      <a href="/wiki/Epicenter" title="Epicenter">
       epicenter
      </a>
      about 23 miles (37 km) south of Bakersfield, measuring 7.3 on the
      <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">
       Richter scale
      </a>
      killed 12 people. In addition to the deaths, it was responsible for at least 18 injuries and more than $60 million in property damage. The main shock was felt over much of California and as far away as Phoenix, Arizona and Reno, Nevada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenwood_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greenwood-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The earthquake occurred on the White Wolf Fault and was the strongest to occur in California since the
      <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">
       1906 San Francisco earthquake
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi,_California" title="Tehachapi, California">
       Tehachapi
      </a>
      suffered the greatest damage and loss of life from the earthquake, though its effects were widely felt throughout central and southern California. The event had a significant
      <a href="/wiki/Aftershock" title="Aftershock">
       aftershock
      </a>
      sequence that persisted into July and August with the strongest coming on August 22, an M5.8 event with a maximum perceived intensity of VIII (Severe) and resulted in two additional deaths and an additional $10 million in property damage. Repercussions of the sequence of earthquakes were still being felt in the heavily damaged downtown area of Bakersfield well into the 1990s as city leaders attempted to improve safety of the surviving non-reinforced masonry buildings.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the event, a field survey was conducted along the fault zone with the goal of estimating the peak ground acceleration of the shock based on visually evaluating precarious rock formations and other indicators. Ground disturbances that were created by the earthquakes were also surveyed, both in the valley and in the foothills, with both vertical and horizontal displacements present in the epicenter area. The strong motion records that were acquired from the event were significant, and a reconnaissance report was recognized for its coverage of the event, and how it set a standard for those types of engineering or scientific papers.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Abuse_trials">
       Abuse trials
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Abuse trials">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Between 1983 and 1986, several ritual sex ring
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kern_county_child_abuse_cases" title="Kern county child abuse cases">
       child abuse cases
      </a>
      occurred in Kern County, resulting in numerous long prison sentences, all of which were overturned—some of them decades later, because the prosecutors had coerced false testimonies from the purported child victims.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mean_Justice.27s_Dirty_Secrets.2C_Rolling_Stone_Magazine_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mean_Justice.27s_Dirty_Secrets.2C_Rolling_Stone_Magazine-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The details of these false accusations are covered extensively in the 2008 documentary
      <i>
       Witch Hunt
      </i>
      , narrated by
      <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">
       Sean Penn
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_Film">
       Music and Film
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Music and Film">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Kern county is considered to be a hotbed of country music, specifically the
      <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield_sound" title="Bakersfield sound">
       Bakersfield sound
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Buck_Owens_Crystal_Palace" title="Buck Owens Crystal Palace">
       Buck Owens Crystal Palace
      </a>
      is located in Bakersfield.
     </p>
     <p>
      The 2015
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">
       Disney
      </a>
      film
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McFarland_(2014_film)" title="McFarland (2014 film)">
        McFarland, USA
       </a>
      </i>
      , starring
      <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Costner" title="Kevin Costner">
       Kevin Costner
      </a>
      , is based on the cross-country team in the town of
      <a href="/wiki/McFarland,_California" title="McFarland, California">
       McFarland, California
      </a>
      , which is located in northern Kern County.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
       Geography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      According to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">
       U.S. Census Bureau
      </a>
      , the county has a total area of 8,163 square miles (21,140 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ), of which 8,132 square miles (21,060 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) is land and 31 square miles (80 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) (0.4%) is water.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GR1-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is the third-largest county by area in California. Its area is nearly the size of the state of
      <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">
       New Hampshire
      </a>
      ; it extends:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       East beyond the southern slope of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">
        Sierra Nevada range
       </a>
       into the
       <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">
        Mojave Desert
       </a>
       , and includes parts of the Indian Wells Valley and
       <a href="/wiki/Antelope_Valley" title="Antelope Valley">
        Antelope Valley
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       West from the Sierra across the floor of the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">
        San Joaquin Valley
       </a>
       to the eastern edge of the
       <a href="/wiki/Temblor_Range" title="Temblor Range">
        Temblor Range
       </a>
       , part of the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Coast_Ranges" title="California Coast Ranges">
        Coast Ranges
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       South over the ridge of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi_Mountains" title="Tehachapi Mountains">
        Tehachapi Mountains
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetation">
       Vegetation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vegetation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Chaparral" title="Chaparral">
       Chaparral
      </a>
      comprises a considerable portion of the natural area within Kern County; the species diversity within these chaparral habitats, however, is considerably less than in many other regions of California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Whitethorn,_California" title="Whitethorn, California">
       Whitethorn, California
      </a>
      is a prominent example of chaparral species on the rocky slopes of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">
       Sierra Nevada
      </a>
      as well as the Inner Coastal Ranges.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Buckeye" title="California Buckeye">
       California Buckeye
      </a>
      is a notable tree found in both chaparral and forests and whose southern range terminates in Kern County.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_populated_places_in_Kern_County,_California" title="List of populated places in Kern County, California">
       List of populated places in Kern County, California
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
       2010 United States Census
      </a>
      , Kern County's population was 839,631.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-QF-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was the eleventh-largest county by population in California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">
       center of population
      </a>
      of California is located in Kern County, in the town of
      <a href="/wiki/Buttonwillow,_California" title="Buttonwillow, California">
       Buttonwillow
      </a>
      <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ngs.noaa.gov/INFO/COP/ca_links.htm" rel="nofollow">
       [3]
      </a>
      .
     </p>

          [20]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </th>
       <td colspan="2">
        $52,041
       </td>
      </tr>

     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
       2010 United States Census
      </a>
      reported that Kern County had a population of 839,631. The racial makeup of Kern County was 499,766 (59.5%)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">
       White
      </a>
      , 48,921 (5.8%)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">
       African American
      </a>
      , 12,676 (1.5%)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">
       Native American
      </a>
      , 34,846 (4.2%)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">
       Asian
      </a>
      , 1,252 (0.1%)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">
       Pacific Islander
      </a>
      , 204,314 (24.3%) from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       other races
      </a>
      , and 37,856 (4.5%) from two or more races.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">
       Hispanic
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">
       Latino
      </a>
      of any race were 413,033 persons (49.2%); 43.4% of Kern County residents are of Mexican heritage, 1.0% Salvadoran, 0.5% Colombian, and 0.4% Guatemalan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2000">
       2000
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2000">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      According to the census
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR8_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GR8-32">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
      of 2000, there were 661,645 people, 208,652 households, and 156,489 families residing in the county. The population density was 81 people per square mile (31/km²). There were 231,564 housing units at an average density of 28 per square mile (11/km²). The racial makeup of the county was 61.6%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       White
      </a>
      , 6.0%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Black
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       African American
      </a>
      , 3.4%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Asian
      </a>
      , 1.5%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Native American
      </a>
      , 0.2%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Pacific Islander
      </a>
      , 23.2% from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       other races
      </a>
      , and 4.1% from two or more races. 38.4% of the population were
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Hispanic
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">
       Latino
      </a>
      of any race. 8.4% were of German, 7.2% American and 5.7% Irish ancestry according to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_2000" title="Census 2000">
       Census 2000
      </a>
      . 66.8% spoke English, 29.1% Spanish and 1.0%
      <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">
       Tagalog
      </a>
      as their first language.
     </p>
     <p>
      There were 208,652 households out of which 42.2% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 54.6% were married couples living together, 14.5% had a female householder with no husband present, and 25.0% were non-families. 20.3% of all households were made up of individuals and 7.8% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 3.03 and the average family size was 3.50.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the county the age distribution of the population shows 31.9% under the age of 18, 10.2% from 18 to 24, 29.8% from 25 to 44, 18.7% from 45 to 64, and 9.4% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 31 years. For every 100 females there were 105.3 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 105.3 males.
     </p>
     <p>
      The median income for a household in the county was $35,446, and the median income for a family was $39,403. Males had a median income of $38,097 versus $25,876 for females. The
      <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">
       per capita income
      </a>
      for the county was $15,760. About 16.8% of families and 20.8% of the population were below the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">
       poverty line
      </a>
      , including 27.8% of those under age 18 and 10.5% of those age 65 or over.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Racial_and_ethnic_identity">
       Racial and ethnic identity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Racial and ethnic identity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data.com_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-city-data.com-33">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       White Non-Hispanic (49.5%)
      </li>
      <li>
       Hispanic (38.4%)
      </li>
      <li>
       Other race (23.2%)
      </li>
      <li>
       Black (6.0%)
      </li>
      <li>
       Two or more races (4.1%)
      </li>
      <li>
       American Indian (2.6%)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      (Total can be greater than 100% because Hispanics may be counted in any race.)
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_statistical_area">
       Metropolitan statistical area
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Metropolitan statistical area">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="United States Office of Management and Budget">
       United States Office of Management and Budget
      </a>
      has designated Kern County as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_CA_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Bakersfield, CA Metropolitan Statistical Area">
       Bakersfield, CA Metropolitan Statistical Area
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMB_13-01_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OMB_13-01-34">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">
       United States Census Bureau
      </a>
      ranked the Bakersfield, CA Metropolitan Statistical Area as the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
       63rd most populous
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
       metropolitan statistical area
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_primary_statistical_areas" title="List of United States primary statistical areas">
       68th most populous
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_primary_statistical_area" title="United States primary statistical area">
       primary statistical area
      </a>
      of the United States as of July 1, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-35">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCSA_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PopEstCSA-36">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_safety">
       Public safety
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Public safety">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Fire protection within the county is provided by the
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_County_Fire_Department" title="Kern County Fire Department">
       Kern County Fire Department
      </a>
      . Law enforcement within the county is provided by the
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_County_Sheriff%27s_Department" title="Kern County Sheriff's Department">
       Kern County Sheriff's Department
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fire">
       Fire
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fire">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_County_Fire_Department" title="Kern County Fire Department">
       Kern County Fire Department
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Kern County Fire Department (KCFD) is the agency that provides fire protection and emergency medical services for the county of Kern, California, USA. Over 625 permanent employees and 100 extra help employees protect an area which spans over 8,000 square miles (21,000 km2). KCFD provides fire protection services for over 500,000 citizens living in the unincorporated areas of Kern County and the cities of Arvin, Delano, Maricopa, McFarland, Ridgecrest, Shafter, Taft, Tehachapi and Wasco. This agency is contracted to provide dispatch services for the California City Fire Department, Kern Ambulance based in Wasco, and Care Ambulance based in Lake Isabella. Over 546 uniformed firefighters are stationed in 46 fire stations throughout the county.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sheriff.27s_Office">
       Sheriff's Office
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sheriff's Office">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_County_Sheriff%27s_Department" title="Kern County Sheriff's Department">
       Kern County Sheriff's Department
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Kern County Sheriff's Department is the agency responsible for law enforcement within the County of Kern. The department provides law enforcement within the county, maintains the jails used by both the county and municipal cities, and provides search and rescue. The department contains over 1,200 sworn officers and civilian employees. Its jurisdiction contains all of the unincorporated areas of Kern County, approximately 8,000 square miles. The department headquarters is located at 1350 Norris Road in Bakersfield. There are 15 additional substations located throughout the county. The metro patrol area is divided into four regions: north, south, east, and west.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2009, the county prosecutor claimed “the highest per capita prison commitment rate of any major California County.” Among those convicted were many charged with crimes against children during a
      <a href="/wiki/Moral_panic" title="Moral panic">
       moral panic
      </a>
      . Many of these have since been released. The county is amongst the most prolific with the death penalty assigning
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty">
       death penalty
      </a>
      sentences in 26 cases since 1976. In 2015 Kern County policemen from all departments killed more people per capita than any other American county.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2015, it was revealed that the Kern County Sheriff's office engaged in a longstanding program of attempted cash payoffs to women who had accused deputies of sexual assault. Also in 2015, a civil lawsuit filed by a survivor of a sexual assault committed by Kern County Sheriff's deputy Gabriel Lopez, was settled for $1 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal">
       Federal
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Federal">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:1em 0 1em 1em; font-size:95%;">
      <caption>

     <p>
      Kern is a strongly
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican
      </a>
      county in
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
       Presidential
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       congressional
      </a>
      elections. The last Democratic candidate for President to win a majority in the county was
      <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">
       Lyndon Johnson
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1964" title="United States presidential election, 1964">
       1964
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">
       United States House of Representatives
      </a>
      , Kern County is split between
      <a href="/wiki/California%27s_21st_congressional_district" title="California's 21st congressional district">
       California's 21st congressional district
      </a>
      , represented by
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Valadao" title="David Valadao">
       David Valadao
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/California%27s_23rd_congressional_district" title="California's 23rd congressional district">
       California's 23rd congressional district
      </a>
      , represented by
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Kevin_McCarthy_(California_politician)" title="Kevin McCarthy (California politician)">
       Kevin McCarthy
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="State">
       State
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: State">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly" title="California State Assembly">
       State Assembly
      </a>
      , Kern County is split between the following four Assembly districts:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_26th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 26th State Assembly district">
        the 26th Assembly District
       </a>
       , represented by
       <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">
        Republican
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Devon_Mathis" title="Devon Mathis">
        Devon Mathis
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_32nd_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 32nd State Assembly district">
        the 32nd Assembly District
       </a>
       , represented by
       <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">
        Democrat
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Salas" title="Rudy Salas">
        Rudy Salas
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_34th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 34th State Assembly district">
        the 34th Assembly District
       </a>
       , represented by
       <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">
        Republican
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Grove" title="Shannon Grove">
        Shannon Grove
       </a>
       , and
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/California%27s_36th_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 36th State Assembly district">
        the 36th Assembly District
       </a>
       , represented by
       <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">
        Republican
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Lackey" title="Tom Lackey">
        Tom Lackey
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate" title="California State Senate">
       State Senate
      </a>
      , Kern County is split between
      <a href="/wiki/California%27s_14th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 14th State Senate district">
       the 14th Senate District
      </a>
      , represented by
      <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">
       Republican
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Andy_Vidak" title="Andy Vidak">
       Andy Vidak
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/California%27s_16th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 16th State Senate district">
       the 16th Senate District
      </a>
      , represented by
      <a href="/wiki/California_Republican_Party" title="California Republican Party">
       Republican
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Jean_Fuller" title="Jean Fuller">
       Jean Fuller
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On Nov. 4, 2008 Kern County voted 75.5% in favor of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proposition_8" title="Proposition 8">
       Proposition 8
      </a>
      , which amended the California Constitution to ban same-sex marriages.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="County">
       County
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: County">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Kern County is governed by a five-member
      <a href="/wiki/Board_of_supervisors" title="Board of supervisors">
       board of supervisors
      </a>
      . As of 2015, they are:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1st District, Mick Gleason.
      </li>
      <li>
       2nd District, Zack Scrivner.
      </li>
      <li>
       3rd District, Mike Maggard.
      </li>
      <li>
       4th District, David Couch.
      </li>
      <li>
       5th District, Leticia Perez.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
       Crime
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Crime">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Kern County also holds the distinction of having the most deaths per capita in the US by police shooting per an article published in
      <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">
       The Guardian
      </a>
      on 1 December 2015. In 2015 to the date of publication of the article, there have been 13 deaths by police shootings in a county of less than 875,000 population.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The following table includes the number of incidents reported and the rate per 1,000 persons for each type of offense.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="General">
       General
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: General">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The county has a large agricultural base and is a significant producer of oil,
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
       natural gas
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">
       hydro-electric power
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">
       wind turbine
      </a>
      power and
      <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power" title="Geothermal power">
       geothermal power
      </a>
      . Kern County is a hub of various power sources. The county accounts for one-tenth of overall U.S. oil production, and three of the five largest U.S.
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">
       oil fields
      </a>
      are in Kern County. Kern is also noted for its
      <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">
       mineral
      </a>
      wealth, including
      <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
       gold
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Borate" title="Borate">
       borate
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Kernite" title="Kernite">
       kernite
      </a>
      . The largest
      <a href="/wiki/Open-pit_mining" title="Open-pit mining">
       open pit
      </a>
      mine in California, which mines
      <a href="/wiki/Borax" title="Borax">
       borax
      </a>
      , is at
      <a href="/wiki/Boron,_California" title="Boron, California">
       Boron
      </a>
      in Kern County.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rio_Tinto_Borax_home_page_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rio_Tinto_Borax_home_page-48">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Petroleum">
       Petroleum
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Petroleum">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      As of 2009
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , Kern is California's top oil-producing county, with 81% of the state's 52,144 active
      <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">
       oil wells
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2008rpt_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-2008rpt-49">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_and_development">
       Discovery and development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Discovery and development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Oil development began with the 1894 discovery of the
      <a href="/wiki/Midway-Sunset_Oil_Field" title="Midway-Sunset Oil Field">
       Midway-Sunset Oil Field
      </a>
      , now the third-largest in the United States, in the southwestern portion of Kern County near Maricopa. Yet it was an 1899 discovery along the Kern River, today part of the giant
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_River_Oil_Field" title="Kern River Oil Field">
       Kern River Oil Field
      </a>
      , that was the breakthrough in Kern's oil production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Oil was refined here even before the establishment of the county.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Buena Vista Petroleum Company was organized and incorporated in 1864.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Soon thereafter a refinery was built that operated until April 1867 when work ceased because of high freight charges.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historic_7-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Historic-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was in the Midway-Sunset Oil Field that well drillers brought about the 1910
      <a href="/wiki/Lakeview_Gusher" title="Lakeview Gusher">
       Lakeview Gusher
      </a>
      , the largest recorded
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_gusher" title="Oil gusher">
       oil strike
      </a>
      in U.S. history. The well spewed approximately nine million barrels for 18 months onto the adjacent terrain before workers finally were able to cap it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Other big oil fields in southwestern Kern County discovered early in the 20th century include the
      <a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_Oil_Field" title="Buena Vista Oil Field">
       Buena Vista
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Belridge_Oil_Field" title="South Belridge Oil Field">
       South Belridge
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Cymric_Oil_Field" title="Cymric Oil Field">
       Cymric
      </a>
      fields. The latter is the fastest-growing field in California in terms of barrels produced per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservation_p._2_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conservation_p._2-52">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Later large fields include the
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_River_Oil_Field" title="Kern River Oil Field">
       Kern River Oil Field
      </a>
      , the fifth-largest in the U.S., the adjacent
      <a href="/wiki/Kern_Front_Oil_Field" title="Kern Front Oil Field">
       Kern Front Oil Field
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Poso_Oil_Field" title="Mount Poso Oil Field">
       Mount Poso Oil Field
      </a>
      in the lower foothills of the Sierra north-northeast of Bakersfield and the
      <a href="/wiki/Fruitvale_Oil_Field" title="Fruitvale Oil Field">
       Fruitvale Oil Field
      </a>
      , which underlies much of the city of Bakersfield, along and north of the Kern River.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hluza_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hluza-53">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 22, 2009,
      <a href="/wiki/Occidental_Petroleum" title="Occidental Petroleum">
       Occidental Petroleum
      </a>
      announced it had discovered the equivalent of 150 million to 250 million barrels of oil in Kern County, which the company called the largest oil discovery in California in 35 years. The find added about 10 percent to California's known reserves. Occidental's Ray Irani said it is likely that more oil would be found in the areas outside the initial six wells that tapped the discovery. Occidental has not revealed the exact location of the find, two-thirds of which is natural gas. BNET, an industry web publication, said the find would add to the company's 708 million barrels of proven reserves in California.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Petroleum_today">
       Petroleum today
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Petroleum today">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The county today contributes more than three-quarters of all the oil produced onshore in California.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservation_p._2_52-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conservation_p._2-52">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some of the large oil fields in Kern County which are still active include:
     </p>
     <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Buena_Vista_Oil_Field" title="Buena Vista Oil Field">
         Buena Vista Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cymric_Oil_Field" title="Cymric Oil Field">
         Cymric Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Edison_Oil_Field" title="Edison Oil Field">
         Edison Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Elk_Hills_Oil_Field" title="Elk Hills Oil Field">
         Elk Hills Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fruitvale_Oil_Field" title="Fruitvale Oil Field">
         Fruitvale Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kern_Front_Oil_Field" title="Kern Front Oil Field">
         Kern Front Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kern_River_Oil_Field" title="Kern River Oil Field">
         Kern River Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lost_Hills_Oil_Field" title="Lost Hills Oil Field">
         Lost Hills Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/McKittrick_Oil_Field" title="McKittrick Oil Field">
         McKittrick Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Midway-Sunset_Oil_Field" title="Midway-Sunset Oil Field">
         Midway-Sunset Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View_Oil_Field" title="Mountain View Oil Field">
         Mountain View Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mount_Poso_Oil_Field" title="Mount Poso Oil Field">
         Mount Poso Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/North_Belridge_Oil_Field" title="North Belridge Oil Field">
         North Belridge Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Round_Mountain_Oil_Field" title="Round Mountain Oil Field">
         Round Mountain Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>

        <a href="/wiki/South_Belridge_Oil_Field" title="South Belridge Oil Field">
         South Belridge Oil Field
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Aviation_and_space">
       Aviation and space
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Aviation and space">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Department of Defense facilities include
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edwards_AFB,_California" title="Edwards AFB, California">
       Edwards Air Force Base
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/China_Lake_Naval_Air_Weapons_Station" title="China Lake Naval Air Weapons Station">
       China Lake Naval Air Weapons Station
      </a>
      . As home to
      <a href="/wiki/Edwards_Air_Force_Base" title="Edwards Air Force Base">
       Edwards Air Force Base
      </a>
      the Air Force's main flight test facility, Kern has been the site of many milestones, including the first
      <a href="/wiki/Bell_X-1" title="Bell X-1">
       supersonic flight
      </a>
      and the first landing of the
      <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
       Space Shuttle
      </a>
      . The base has brought prosperity to the railroad towns of
      <a href="/wiki/Mojave,_California" title="Mojave, California">
       Mojave
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rosamond,_California" title="Rosamond, California">
       Rosamond
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kern County is also the home of the first inland spaceport in the United States, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mojave_Spaceport" title="Mojave Spaceport">
       Mojave Spaceport
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_pollution">
       Air pollution
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Air pollution">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="2200" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg/200px-PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg/300px-PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg/400px-PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PM_25_Kern_County_Bakersfield_over_time.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Particulate pollution in Kern County varies with the seasons.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Kern County suffers from severe air pollution. Particulates cause poor visibility, especially in the winter. Western Kern County lies in the
      <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">
       San Joaquin Valley
      </a>
      and the topography traps pollutants. Although the topography is not as unfavorable in eastern Kern County, eastern Kern County is a
      <a href="/wiki/Non-attainment_area" title="Non-attainment area">
       non-attainment area
      </a>
      for particulates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">
       Public transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Public transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arvin_Transit" title="Arvin Transit">
        Arvin Transit
       </a>
       is the local municipal bus operator in and around Arvin.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Delano_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Delano Area Rapid Transit">
        Delano Area Rapid Transit
       </a>
       is the local municipal bus operator in Delano.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Empire_Transit" title="Golden Empire Transit">
        Golden Empire Transit
       </a>
       is the local bus operator in and near Bakersfield.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kern_Regional_Transit" title="Kern Regional Transit">
        Kern Regional Transit
       </a>
       provides countywide
       <a href="/wiki/Intercity_bus_service" title="Intercity bus service">
        intercity bus service
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Taft_Area_Transit" title="Taft Area Transit">
        Taft Area Transit
       </a>
       is the local municipal bus operator in and around Taft.
      </li>
      <li>
       Kern County is also served by
       <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">
        Greyhound
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Orange_Belt_Stages" title="Orange Belt Stages">
        Orange Belt Stages
       </a>
       buses and
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       trains.
      </li>
     </ul>

      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi_Municipal_Airport" title="Tehachapi Municipal Airport">
        Tehachapi Municipal Airport
       </a>
       , Tehachapi. (IATA: TSP)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Wasco_Airport" title="Wasco Airport">
        Wasco Airport
       </a>
       , Wasco. (FAA: L19)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">
       Recreation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kern_County,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Recreation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Among the outdoor recreational activities are horseback riding, water skiing (Lake Buena Vista, Lake Ming, and private ski ranches), off-road biking and dune buggies (
      <a href="/wiki/Jawbone_Canyon" title="Jawbone Canyon">
       Jawbone Canyon
      </a>
      , California City and Randsburg), auto racing (Willow Springs, Buttonwillow, Bakersfield Speedway, Famoso, and an unnamed half-mile speedway under construction), hunting, paint-ball courses, white-water rafting, kayaking, snow skiing (Shirley Meadows and
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pinos" title="Mount Pinos">
       Mount Pinos
      </a>
      ), shooting ranges (5 Dogs Range), hiking, biking (trails, paths, and roads), camping and fishing.
     </p>
